                         Annex 4: Access to Cotton Inputsand Input Policies

IntegratedInput Supply-Output Marketing Model

 1.     The timely use of seeds and fertilizers in optimal quantities has been and still is an
important determinant of improved cotton productivity and quality. The cotton sector in
Burkina Faso is organized around cotton companies which intervene along the various segments
o f the value chain: input supply, extension services, purchase and transport of seed cotton,
ginning and selling of lint cotton. The integrated structure of the cotton sector is to ensure that
these key functions are efficiently executed under the conditions o f small scale family-based
production systems. The functioning o f the cotton industry following an integrated model i s
included in a protocol between the State and the sector's stakeholders since 2004 when the
production has been reorganized around three companies with regional monopoly power
(SOFITEX, SOCOMA and Faso Coton).

2.      The integrated model has well known advantages and disadvantages. Advantages
include: (i)  easiness o f access o f all cotton producers to inputs o f adequate quantity and quality;
(ii)availability oninputsthat are suitable to cottonproduction; (iii)reductionofproduction
costs, including transport, through economies o f scale and scope (e.g. combining input delivery
and seed cotton removal); (iv) establishment o f informal contractual agreements between cotton
producers and cotton companies; and (v) opportunities to improve productivity o f other crops in
the production system.

3.      Disadvantagesinclude: (i)      reduction inrecommended doses o f fertilizer on cotton to the
profit o f other crops not covered by the input distribution system; this i s particularly the case o f
imported fertilizer for which average use per ha fell from 200kg/ha ten years ago to 170kg/ha,
and then to 150kgha duringthe 2008/09 cropping season; (ii) of motivation to produce or
                                                                     lack
to use organic matters in production; (iii)reduction in cotton yield; over-indebtedness o f
producers and their organizations when cotton production is insufficient to cover input costs,
which explains internal and external debts to the groups o f cotton producers; (iv) increases in
financing needs and financial charges o f cotton companies, leading to difficulties in mobilizing
additional resources to purchase seed cotton and inputs in response to increased production; (v)
surcharges in input prices paid by producers by at least 20%, according to information obtained
from cotton companies.

Input Policies

4.      The cotton crisis stemming from the collapse of world prices in 2004/05 and the
recent global financial crisis exacerbated the drawbacks of the integrated structure of the
cotton sector whereby input supply functions are combined with cotton seed ginning and lint
marketing functions in the industry. The cumulated deficits o f the three cotton companies have
ledto the deteriorationo ftheir financial situation to the point that they face difficulties to finance
additional purchase o f seed cotton, and obtaining inputs for the 2010/11 cropping season.
Adopting o f a new input distribution policy i s today an urgency. This policy will aim to perverse
the advantages of the integrated system on a sustainable basis while eliminating the
disadvantages, particularly the high financial charges incurred in the current system, the
increasing input cost paid by producers and the associated reduction in fertilizer doses and
productivity loss, the last of interest inthe large scale use o f organic fertilizer.


                                                  - 75 -

5.       The Government could support the new input system by adopting three
complementary actions: (i)the creation of an input fund which would lead to at least 20%
reduction in input costs for producers, and reduce the financial need of cotton companies by
30%; (ii)   the revision of existing input formula, which are increasingly inadequate to deal with
increased soil acidification in cotton zones; (iii)           the financing of programs to encourage large
scale adoption and use of manure and green matters to restore soil fertility. Supporting these
actions could also help solve the recurrent problem of cotton input subsidies faced by the
Government. The subsidies are estimated to more than CFAF23 billion since 2003, and could
amount to CFAF7-8 billion per year over the coming years should fertilizer prices stay at 50%
higher thanthe 2000 price levels

Impact of the Creation of an Input Fund on Incomes and Poverty

6.       The impact of the creation of an input fund on incomes and poverty is measuredby
combining partial budget for average cotton farms with nationally representative household
survey data. Based on the characteristics of cotton farmers, the average cotton acreage was 4ha
in 2005/06 and 2006/07, but sharply fell to 2.7ha in 2007/08. This analysis is based on the
average cotton acreage of 3ha per household. The assumed household size incotton zones is 12,
which is based on survey data (Table A4.1). Total input cost excluding seeds averaged
CFAF75,OOO per ha during the 2005/06 and 2006/07 cropping seasons (Tables A4.2 and A4.3) .
The reduction in input costs associated with the creation of the input fund i s based on the
CFAF75,OOO average per ha input costs excluding seeds). Based on the financial arrangements
by cotton companies and input supplier             joy   it was determinedthat potential cost savings would
amount to between20% and 30% ofthe CFAF75,000/ha base.




    Source: Staf estimates based SOFITWINERA data

7.       Given the current characteristics of the cotton input supply systems, and given the
potential economies that may be realized through savings on financial charges, the creation of
input fund will help improve the profitability of cotton production at farm level. Gross
margin is expected to increase by CFAFl5-22,500kaYor CFAF45-67,500 per household. Given
the relatively large family size, the per capita gains are estimated between CFAF3,750 and

                                                        - 77 -

8.      In general, the household level benefits from the input fund will increasewith the
size of cotton acreage. This i s typical to area-based or volume-based subsidies, which tend to
provide the largest benefits to larger and often richer producers. Thus, the intervention will
unambiguously reduce poverty across large and small farm households, but its poverty targeting
efficiency may not be optimal. The choice to create an input fundmay still bejustified on several
other grounds, even if it does not deliver superior pro-poor outcomes. The reason is that cotton
continues to be an important engine for growth, and that large cotton farmers continue to play a
significant food security role in the economy. It i s often said that cotton producers are also the
largest food crop producers. Cotton farmers are net sellers of grains for both rural net food
buyers and urban dwellers. Some of the cereals, particularly maize, is commercialized at regional
level within what is now known as the West African maize basin covering more than 10
countries.




                                              - 78 -

   Annex 5: StructureandDeterminantsof InternalDebtto CottonProducers'Group in
                                          BurkinaFaso

1.      An internal debt is owed to producers by producers. Producers obtain cotton input
credit as membersof a village level cotton producers' group, known as GPC. Credit is extended
to GPCs, and all members are collectively responsible of the loan according group lending
principles. Generally, GPC members have close affinity and have less incentive to willfully
default on credit, which substantially limits moral hazard risks. There i s however a residual risk
of default, which tends to be exacerbated by climatic shocks. The Burkina national cotton
producers' union (UNPCB) conducted a survey in late 2008 to establish the level of the internal
debts. Estimates indicate that total internal debt amounted to CFAF 4.4 billions (more than $8
million). Approximately two-third of this amount was accumulated during the 2007-08 cropping
season, when cotton production suffered from an unexpected flood toward the need of the
production cycle.

2.      Historically, Burkina Faso has launched a cotton sector revival strategy in 1995-1996.
Several actions were supportedunder this strategy. These include improving the efficiency of the
group lending system and reinforcing the governance structure of the village groups, which later
will be known as GPCs. The strategy also supported the clearance of CFAF2 billions ininternal
debts of the village groups, which contributed to increase production from 147,000 tons in
1995/96to 214,000 tons in 1996/97 and further to 338,000 tons in 1997/98. While these reforms
helped bring many farmers back to cotton production, they have also contributed to transfer a
greater share of input credit default risks from the cotton company (SOFITEX) to GPCs. The
system worked relatively well until recently when the 2006/07 drought and the 2007/08 flood
contributed to worsen the GPCs' internal debt crisis.

3.      The relationship between climatic shocks and GPC debts can be understood by
analyzing the historical data on the cotton average yield and producer's debts (Figure A4.1). In
general, a nationally averaged cotton yield will display little inter-annual variation because of
offsetting climatic effects across the national territory. However, in the event of a widespread
system shock, aggregated yield could be affected. Since early 2000, nationwide seed cotton
yield averaged 1,058kg. But yield dropped by 14% to 909kg in 2006/07, mainly to widespread
floods in cotton production zones. This resulted in substantial loss of early maturing capsules.
Yield performance deteriorated further to 851kg per ha (20% of the 200-05 average) in2007/08
following when rains stopped prematurely (Figure A5.1). At the same time, internal arrears
surged from CFAF1.5 to CFAF4.4 billion.

4.      The problem of internal debts of cotton producers groups represents a serious
threat to the sustainability of cotton production in Burkina Faso. The full scale of the
problem is yet to be observed. However, there i s already good evidence that farmers may be
responding to the higher risk of peer default by exiting cotton production or at least drastically
reducing their cropping areas under cotton. According to the most recent figures in 2009 from
the Cotton Producers Union (UNPCB), there are 325,000 cotton farmers, and 11,889 cotton
producers groups inBurkina Faso. The Unionhas also commissioned a study that establishedthe
exhaustive list of producers affected by the problem, and the volume of outstanding debts owed
by some cotton producers to other producers. However, the study was limited to producers who
had unpaid balance vis-a-vis their GPC. The study's estimates show that there are 22,527


                                              - 79 -

producers from 6,521 GPCs who can be considered to belong to the group o f debtors. This
represents approximately 7% o fproducers and 55% o f GPCs.

5.      But the situation may be more complicated than initially thought, as confirmed
during discussions with the sector's stakeholders and with GPCs visited (Box A5.1). One o f the
three cotton company, Faso Coton (with 5 percent o f the market share), reported that one inthree
producers are debtors vis-a-vis other members o f their GPCs. Faso 'Coton controls a cotton
production zone more prone to drought, and it i s estimated that 30% o f farmers have stopped
cotton production due to the problem o f internal debts. Most o f these farmers are among the best
performers, increasing the risks o f reduced overall cotton production, reduced profitability of
cotton companies, and reduced export earnings.

6.      SOFITEX (85% market share) has also carried out a light survey of 122 producers and
76 GPCs in 17 villages representing all cotton production zones covered by the company. The
survey also revealed that the average GPC size fell from 33 in 2005/06 to 29 in 2008109. This
reduction in GPC size by 11 percent between the two periods i s attributed to the increased
difficulties faced by cotton producers. More generally, the survey has provided materials to
examine the preliminary structure, characteristics and determinants o f internal debts in cotton
production in the SOFITEX zone. The results show that four in five GPCs are confronted with
the problem o f debts in the SOFITEX zone. Among these, 68% face internal debts only; 4
percent face external arrears only; and 8 percent face both internal and external debts (Figure
A5.2). Under normal circumstances, GPCs that have external arrears (that i s vis-a-vis the cotton
companies) are excluded from input credit benefits. However, the survey reveals that many o f
the indebted GPCs have continued to benefit from these credits, because o f the cumulated
difficulties confionting the cotton sector.

7.      Three groups of producersemerged from the analysis of SOFITEX data. Creditors
(Group l),   representingapproximately one infour producers, appear to be the most loyal cotton
producers. Three infour producers from this group have more than 10 years experience incotton
production. Nine in ten have been producing cotton for five years or more. This group
represented 22% o f the producers in 2008/09, but has contributed to between 31% and 39% of
total production over the last three cropping seasons (Tables A5.1 & A5.4). Cotton farms inthis
group averaged 5.5ha in size between2005/06 and 2006/07, before dropping drastically to 3.7ha
in2007/08. Average cottonproduction is also highest inthis group, andso are the areas allocated
to non-cotton crops.

10.     SOFITEX has a farmers' monitoringsystem which categorizes producers into four
groups based on their farm equipment. The use of animal traction is widespread in cotton
production zones, and the norm for producers i s to have a complete set o f equipment, including
the traction animal and the related tilling, weeding, and transport equipment. When a farmer
meets these conditions, he or she is classified as equipped. Some farmers do not have all these
equipment and are therefore classified as incompletely equipped. If, in addition to being fully
equipped, the farmer has a motorized traction, she is classified as such, and so are farmers with
animal traction equipment. Based on the light survey results, there appears to be a strong
correlation between debtors (Group 3) and lack o f animal traction use in cotton production.
Nearly half o f cotton producers belonging to this group have no animal traction equipment, as
compared to nearly one third (30%) for creditors and slightly more than one-quarter (26%) for
producers unaffected by the internal debt. To minimize risks o f future default, it will be
necessary to explore restrictions that can be placed on access to credit for farmers with no
equipment.

11.     Regression analyses confirm the strong links between lack of complete equipment
sets and the presence of internal debts at household level. The use on animal or motorized
traction significantly decrease to probability o f falling into debt by 12 to 15 percentage points
according to marginal probability analyses (Table A5-6).

12.     In summary, it can be noted that a significant proportion o f internal GPC debt has been
accumulated over the last few cropping cycles and appears to be closely associated with
occurrence o f adverse climatic events.      In line with existing rules o f the game governing
repayment o f GPC debts, it i s the surplus farmers who ultimately pay for the debts o ftheir fellow
GPC member who are in deficit. It i s well-known within GPCs who are surplus- and who are
deficit- farmers. To the extent that GPC membership is made up o f various extended family-
based subgroups, arrangements have been put inplace within GPCs to settle internal debts at the

                                                - 83 -

sub-group level. There is a significant risk that surplus farmers might abandoncotton cultivation,
thereby causing a potentially disproportionate reduction inoverall production volumes that might
further hurt processing capacity utilization ratios, thereby further undermining the
competitiveness of cotton firms. In view of this, there is a need to resolve internal GPC debt
while at the same time avoiding moral hazard. One action to be consideredis to provide an input
package free of charge to GPCs with the cost of the package equaling the existing internal debt
of the group. Because of GPC's internal debt accounting rules it would be surplus farmers who
would benefit from this measure, while at the same time providing an incentive for the above-
average farmers to stay incottonproduction.

            Annex 6: Burkina Faso-IMF Assessment Notefor the World Bank

This note provides an assessmentof recent macroeconomic developments inBurkina
Faso and progress under the Fund-supported three-year Poverty Reduction and Growth
Facility program (PRGF). This assessmenti s based on the findings o f the mission for the
fourth review that took place inOuagadougou March 18-April 1,2009.

RecentEconomicDevelopmentsandProgramPerformance

In 2008 and early 2009, Burkina Faso's economy weathered the triple external shocks
(oil, food, and the global financial crisis) fairly well. Real GDP growth reached an
estimated 5 percent in 2008, supported by a rebound in agricultural production and the
opening o f three new gold mines. With the decline in commodity prices, inflation fell to
6.8 percent year-on-year in March 2009 after peaking at 15.1 percent in June last year.
Domestic food prices, however, have declined less than international prices. The trade
deficit widened to 11.O percent o f GDP, from 8.8 percent in 2007, because o f higher oil
imports and lower cotton exports.

Despite difficult economic conditions, program performance was broadly in line with
objectives. All quantitative performance criteria were met, including the targets for the
fiscal deficit, revenues, and social expenditure. However, foreign-financed capital
expenditure was some 2% percent of GDP lower than programmed, mainly due to poor
project planning and execution and higher costs that required renegotiation o f loans.
Despite progress on preparation for tax policy reform, some delays have occurred
because o f late delivery o f technical assistance, inadequate domestic capacity, and the
challenging external context.

OutlookandPolicyChallenges

The global financial crisis influences the near-term outlook and is constraining growth.
Monthly trade indicators and trade-related revenues are slackening. While lower prices
dampen the outlook for cotton exports, the impact on the balance o f payments will be
cushioned by agricultural initiatives, lower oil prices, and higher gold prices. Real GDP
growth i s projected to decline to 3% percent in 2009. Changes in commodity prices are
expected to improve the terms o f trade and slightly narrow the current account deficit.

There are risks to the outlook. Further decline in world cotton prices could threaten the
financial stability o f the ginning companies, which would have negative side-effects for
the entire economy. A worsening global crisis could also further push down remittances,
foreign direct investment, and other financial flows,          lowering investment and
consumption. An unexpectedly fast global recovery would support a turnaround in
Burkina Faso.




                                           - 85 -

Inthis difficult environment, the key challenge is sustain the reform momentum, with a
particular focus on fiscal reforms to raise revenues, and growth-enhancing reforms to
makethe cotton sector more efficient andthe financial sector stronger.

While there is some scope for countercyclical fiscal policy, debt sustainability concerns
call for caution, and grant financing will be especially important in the event that
downside risks to revenue materialize. Medium-term fiscal consolidation remains
necessary to reduce the high risk o f debt distress, and while the fiscal deficit on a
commitment basis i s projected to widen to 5.1 percent o f GDP in 2009, it should decline
to 4.1 percent o f GDP by 2011. Preparatory work for tax policy reform is underway with
a view to revise the business tax, streamline tax exemptions, and strengthen VAT.

In the cotton sector, though financing for the next campaign has been secured on
conditions similar to last year's, the capital base o f SOFITEX, the largest ginning
company, i s eroding, and producer association internal arrears have risen. Reforming the
sector i s critical if the country's medium-term growth and development objectives are to
be achieved. The authorities have stressed their commitment to increasing the
transparency and efficiency o f SOFITEX. Staff encouraged the authorities to work
closely with the World Bank and take the necessary steps to increase productivity.

The financial system has so far weathered the global financial storm, but could be
vulnerable to a drying-up o f liquidity, an increase innonperforming loans as the economy
slows, credit concentration, or withdrawal o f foreign banks if disruptions in international
financial markets should intensify. Better surveillance, supervision, and risk management
at both national and regional levels are thus essential. Staff encouraged the authorities to
ensure adequate follow up to the financial sector action plan that was submitted to
Cabinet inMarch2009.

Overall,   we believe that the PRGF-supported program will provide a sound
macroeconomic framework to guide the authorities' reform efforts. Staff will continue to
maintain close coordinationwith donors.

Relations with the IMF

The Executive Board discussion o f the fourth review under the PRGF arrangement i s
scheduled on June 22, and the mission for the 2009 Article IV consultation and fifth
review under the PRGF arrangement i s expected to take place in September.

                                     Annex 7: PRSG-9 Burkina Faso

                             Joint BanWFundDebt SustainabilityAnalysis

                          INTERNATIONAL MONETARY FUNDAND
                       INTERNATIONAL DEVELOPMENT ASSOCIATION

                                            BURKINAFASO

                          Joint Bank/FundDebtSustainabilityAnalysis

               Preparedby the staffs of the International Development Association
                                  andthe International Monetary Fund

                   Approved by Carlos A. Primo Braga and Sudhir Shetty (IDA)
                         and MichaelAtingi-Ego and Anthony Boote (IMF)

                                              May 21,2009


The debt sustainability outlookfor Burkina Faso is aligned with the results of theprevious
debt sustainability analysis @SA) update carried out in November 2008. 32 Despite a clear
increase in projected gold exports in 2010, the medium- and long-term export outlook
deteriorates slightly because exports of cotton are reduced. Burkina Faso is still classi3ed as
a mediumperformer 33 and the country remains at high risk of debt distress.

                                       VII. BACKGROUND

1.       The analysispresentedinthis documentis basedon the stock of BurkinaFaso's
debt at end-2007.The stock of debt was establishedfollowing a creditor-by-creditor and
loan-by-loan reconciliation exercise that was carried out inApril 2008 and showed a
negligible discrepancy betweenthe authorities' and creditors' data. Moreover, the stock of
debt at end-2008 has beenestimatedbased on aggregatedinformationprovided by the
authorities.

2.      BurkinaFaso's externaldebt is composedinthe largestpart by financingfrom
multilateralcreditors,which account for almost 80 percentof the totalof outstanding
loans.The share ofthe World Bankrepresents about one thirdofthe total, that ofthe AfDB
about 15 percent, andthat of the IMF about 3 percent. Loans from bilateral creditors
represent about 20 percent o fthe total, of which about 90 percent were extendedby non-Paris
Club creditors. BurkinaFaso's loans have longmaturities, with anoverall grant element
which currently standsat about 48 percent and is projectedto remainabove 35 percent for


32For thejoint DSA fiom April 2008, see EBS/08/136andAnnex 6 inIDA ReportNo. 4033-BF, August 26,
2008; for the DSA updatefrom November2008 preparedby Fundstaff, see EBS/08/136.The comparisonto
changes since the last DSA refers to the November2008 update, unless otherwise indicated.
33With a three-yearbackwardmovingaverage CPIA for 2005-2007below 3.75.

                                                  - 88 -

the entire projectionperiodo fthe DSA. While there is a gradual decline inthe grant element
to about 37 percent by 2028, this i s explainedfor the most part by a shift inemphasis innew
lendingfrom multilateral to bilateral creditors. With regardto the compositionof external
financing, the grant-financing share amounted to 56 percent in2008.

3.      Since the transitionfrom a centralizedto a market-orientedeconomy inthe
early 1990s,BurkinaFaso's governmenthas consistentlydemonstrateditscommitment
to stay currenton itsexternalpaymentobligations.This includesthe period before the
country benefited from debt reliefunder the Heavily IndebtedPoor Country Initiative
(HIPC), when the NPV o f debt-to-exports ratio was well above 200 percent. The 35 percent
concessionality floor i s strictly enforced for all central-government foreign-currency
borrowings, and projects are consistently scrutinized by a National Public Debt Committee
before negotiations are concluded.

        VIII. UNDERLYINGMACROECONOMIC ASSUMPTIONS

4.      The medium-termoutlookfor growthis generallyunchangedfrom the previous
DSA. Projectionsfor real GDP growth holdover the medium-term, but have been loweredby
1.4 percentage points for 2009 and 1.9 percentage points for 2010 because o fthe slowdown
inglobal demand, including inthe cotton sector. As a result, nominal GDP projectionsare
slightly lower than inthe previous DSA, but the upward trend is clear for the medium and
long term (Figure 1,Panel 1). Real GDP growth i s projected to average 6 percent inthe long
run,broadly inline withthe average for the past tenyears. Inflationisprojectedto decline to
4.8 percent in2009,2.3 percent in2010, and to the historical average o f about 2 percent in
2011.

5.      Fiscal developments over the mediumterm are also alignedwith the previous
DSA.The projected fiscal deficit target for 2009 has been increased by 0.4 percentage points
to 5.3 percent o f GDP to account for the negative impact o fthe global crisis on tax revenues
andthe needto increase some transfer
expenditures. While recognizing how the                   Fiscal Developments,2007-28

                                               - 89 -

6.       Recent commodity price developments warranted a revisionof some projections
on the externalsector comparedto the previousDSA. Inthe near term, the projected
decline incottonprices will be offset by an increase inthe price o f gold and a decline inoil
prices, leading to an improvement inthe terms o f trade o f about 10percent and a narrowing
o fthe current account deficit. The medium term export outlook has beenrevisedfor the
following reasons:

Commodity prices:Cottonpriceshave declinedby about 40 percent since their August 2008 peak;
         they are about 21percent lower for 2009 and 14 percentlower for 2010than the previous
         DSA projected (Figure 1, Panel5). Onthe other hand, gold prices are expectedto be about 29
         percenthigher in2009 and 27 percenthigher in2010.

Exchangerate: The value ofthe US dollar relativeto the CFA franc has beenrevisedupwardby 5.7
         percent, which over the mediumterm reducesthe total value inUS.dollars of Burkina
         Faso's exports.

Medium-termexport potential:The first significant change is a downwardrevision inthe value of
         cotton exports basedon lower export pricesandthe negative impact on supply of the increase
         incotton inventoriesglobally. Dueto the shortage ofarablelands, the shareof cottonexports
         as a percentof GDP is projectedto declinemarkedly over the longterm (Figure 1, Panel2).
         The second importantchange comes from a significant increase inthe volume of gold exports
         in2010, from 10.5 tons inthe previousDSA to 16tons currently,becauseofthe operations
        over the nextten years of anew gold mine. While exploration is underway for additional
        mines, which could leadto a significantly higher gold exports, this is not reflected inthe
        assumptions o fthe currentDSA.A third change concerns the increase from 2015 onward in
        exports of fruits, vegetables and cereals as the authorities' agricultural diversification strategy
        comes into play.


7.      The current account deficitis expected to narrow moderatelyinthe mediumand
longrun as the tighter fiscalstance dampens import demand.Export growth is driven in
the mediumterm bythe projected increase ingold exports in2010 and inthe longterm by
efforts to diversify agricultural production away from cotton and into fmit, vegetables, and
cereals.

           IX. EXTERNAL DEBT SUSTAINABILITY ANALYSIS

8.      There are no significantchangesto the indicatorscomparedto the previousDSA
(Figure 2). Under the baseline scenario, there is a slight deterioration inthe NPV of debt-to-
exports ratio, the only indicator that breaches the indicative thresholds. With the decline in
cotton exports over the long term, the ratio peaks at 196.4percent in2024, comparedto
190.7percent inthe previous DSA.Nevertheless, all other debt indicators remain
comfortably below the thresholds.

9.      Furthermore, the rate of externaldebt accumulationunder the baselinescenario
is projectedto remain manageable.The annual increase inthe NPV of public external debt
i s substantially below 3 percent of GDP per year throughout the projection period and,
notwithstanding a small increase inthe mediumterm, it is projected to remainat about
20 percent of GDP. Additional grant financing could improve the debt sustainability outlook
significantly. Whereas DSA projections are based on a conservative 50 percent grant-
financing share, raising the grant-financing share to 55 percent inthe projection period would
lower the peak NPV of debt-to-exports ratio by about 20 percentagepoints.

10.     Stress tests and alternative scenarios show Burkina Faso's debt outlook as
vulnerable to large shocks to exportsand less favorablefinancingterms. The NPV of
debt-to-exports andthe debt service-to-exports ratios rises and stays above the threshold
under some tests. Inparticular, these ratios are most vulnerable to a scenario of exports
remaining subdued and growing below historical levels (Figure 5). While all the other ratios
remain belowtheir indicative thresholdsthroughout the projection period, stress test show
there are vulnerabilities, inparticular to a combination of lower GDP growth and a lower
share of grants inexternal financing (bounds tests B2 and B5 and alternative scenario A2 in
Table 2, respectively).

                         X. ALTERNATIVE SCENARIOS

11.    How vulnerableis the debt sustainabilityoutlookto further backlashfrom the
current globalcrisis? The baseline scenario o fthe DSA assumes (i)continued
                                                                      a
improvement inrevenue performance to meet the WAEMUtarget o f 17 percent in2015 and
(ii)moderatedeclineintheshareofcottonintotalexportsthatiscompensatedinthe
    a
mediumterm by a significant increase inthe volume andvalue of gold exports.

12.    The alternativescenarioassumesa further declinein projectedrevenue
comparedto precrisislevels, a worseningof the outlookfor cotton, andlowergold
pricesas the globalrecovery startsto take hold:

               Revenues are lower by 0.5 percentage points of GDP inboth 2010 and2011,
               before gradually recovering to their baseline level by 2017.

               Cotton prices are 10 percent lower in2010, returning to the baseline in2011.

               Cotton export volumes are 20 percent lower in2010, an impact that carries
               over into the medium and long runas producers diversify away from the
               sector inresponse to lower prices in2009 and 2010 and declining prospects.

               Gold prices are 10 percent lower in2011and 5 percent lower in2012 and
               2013 before catching up to the baseline level in2014 (Figure 3).

13.    The resultsunderthe alternativescenario do notforesee a significant
deteriorationof the debt sustainabilityoutlook, andmost debt sustainability indicators
would be littleaffectedover the longterm. The indicators remain below their indicative
thresholds for mediumperformers, with the exception o fthe NPV o f debt-to-exports ratio,
which exceeds 200 percent (Figure 4).

                                                                        - 96 -

        XI. PUBLIC SECTOR DEBT SUSTAINABILITY ANALYSIS

14.      The resultsfor the fiscal DSA are similarto those for the externalDSA.Domestic
debt i s low-gross   domestic debt i s estimated at approximately 2.7 percent o f GDP at end-
2008, and net debt at 1.3 percent o f GDP. Moreover, it is assumed to decline further over the
projection period as the authorities seek to avoid more costly domestic financing o f the fiscal
deficit. As a result, public debt dynamics are largely determined by the evolution o f external
debt.

15.      Publicdebt indicatorscouldworsen undersome scenarios. The standard
sensitivity tests reveal the public debt outlook to be vulnerable to persistent large primary
deficits and an unexpected increase indebt creating flows, under which the debt ratios would
increase sharply over the projection period. These results highlight the importanceto follow
prudent fiscal and borrowing policies. Failure to reduce the current deficits would leadto
ever-increasing debt indicators; however the authorities are committed to ongoing tax
reforms designed to lower the deficit to more sustainable levels.

                                    XII. CONCLUSION

16.      BurkinaFaso's riskof debt distress is highbecauseo fthe NPV o fdebt-to-exports
ratio; all other debt indicators remain comfortably below their policy-dependent thresholds in
the baseline scenario. Nevertheless, the highrisk o f distress underscores the importance o f
limiting external borrowing to concessional loans, maintaining a prudent fiscal policy to limit
the accumulationo fnew debt, including by sustaining the ongoing tax reforms, andmaking
continued efforts to diversify and increase exports. Moreover, the authorities should continue
to improve their policy and institutional environment, which over time may result ina higher
CPIA rating andhigher debt thresholds.

                      Annex 11: GeneralBudgetSupportFramework(CGAB-CSLP) -
                                       Definition of Measuresfor 2008

Measures for 2008:


1.      Adopt the 2009 draft appropriation bill based on the overall MTEFsectoral ceilings for 2008-
2010, in accordancewith PRSP priorities: This measure aims at measuring government's determination
to translate into concrete reality its commitment to implement its program to reduce poverty, in keeping
with PRSP priorities. Its implementation shall be assessed on the basis o f a report by the DGB at the
Ministryo fthe Economy and Finance containing a comparative analysis o f CDMT sectoral appropriations
and the draft appropriation bill based on PRSP priorities (inthe Education, Health, Rural Development       ...
sectors).
2.      Design a fiscal policy reform strategy and include in the draft appropriation bill for 2009
short term measures that are in conformity with the guidelines of the said strategy: This measure
aims at scaling down the bases o f most taxes, eliminating taxes that are a burdento businessesand o f low
returnfor tax authorities and simplifying the tax system. The fiscal reform strategy paper adopted by the
Council o f Ministers and the effective implementation o f short term measures in conformity with the
guidelines o f the said strategy laid down in the 2009 finance law will stand as proof that the measure has
been implemented

3.      Set the 2009-2011 MTEF for the health, education, economic, and finance sectors and engage
the experimental MTEF for the judicial sector: MTEFs are programming instruments that make it
possible to clearly see how to implement sectoral programs, in so far as they provide prospects for
resources during a triennial period while at the same time scaling up coherence in the inter sector
allocation o f resource availability for priorities and programs agreed upon in the sectoral strategies and
policies.. Proof as to the implementation o f this measure will be seen through the production o f MTEF
2009-2011 reports validated by the sectors concerned, come December 31,2008

4.      Assess the strategies, policiesand programs of the rural development sector: This activity falls
within the framework o f the plan to design a sectoral program for productive rural development
(PROSDRp). The program aims at ensuring the coherence o f investments in the productive rural sector
(agriculture, animal resources and the living environment and conditions) and at promoting sector
approach at the level o f the rural sector. This measure will be evaluated on the basis o f the availability o f
the assessmentreport.
5.      Design and start the implementation of an urgent plan to scale down the impact of the food
crisis on producers and consumers and revive cereal production: The urgent measures to be
implemented within the framework o f an action plan are geared towards the stabilization o f the
macroeconomic framework and the food security o f the population. The action plan adopted by the
Council o f Ministers on the urgent measures to implement will serve as proof that the measure has been
implemented.
6.      Continue the implementation of the strategy to overcome the crisis and revive the cotton
sector, notably by:

           0    Setting up a consultation framework for players in the cotton sector for the sharing o f
      .     information on the performance o f the strategy to weather the crisis and for exchanges on the
            sector's environment. A government report on the functioning o f the consultation framework
           will constitute proofo f implementationo fthis measure

           0    The strict application by the cotton sector o f the rules and regulations governing
           equalization funds. The fixing o f floor prices for the purchase o f gin cotton and, as the case



                                                      - 114-

            may be, drawbacks for the 2008-2009 season based on the method of calculation adopted by
            the equalization fund will constituteproofof implementation ofthismeasure;

            0   The taking by SOFITEX, in a bid to showcase itself to potential investors, of measures
            aimed at improving businessgovernance and its efficiency, notably through i)the pursuit of the
            implementation of the plan to curb its operation cost; ii)the start of the implementation of the
            relevant recommendations of the ongoing operational and financial audit; iii)the presentation
            of certified accounts for 2008 containing fewer reservations than those in the certified accounts
            for 2007. Proof of implementation of these measures will be shown via a SOFITEX report on
            the extent of implementation of the structural adjustment plan, the board of directors' decision
            on the audit recommendationsand through the 2008 accounts certification report.

            The assurance by the State of the availability of fertilizers and seeds for all producers during
            the 2008-2009 season. A SP-SFCL report indicating that fertilizers and seeds have beenplaced
            at the disposal of producerswill be a proof of implementation ofthis measure;

            Rating advice to SOFITEX by a rating agency. Proofof implementation of this measurewill be
            attestedby a document showing the signing of a bid contractwith the agency.


7.       Have adopted by the Councilof Ministersand submit to the National Assembly the legaland
regulatory texts on the ITC sector: Attention will bepaid inthis regardto electronic signature and to the
decree on the procedure for certifying electronic signatures. The dispatch note of the draft bill to
Parliament and the minutes of the Council of Ministers' meeting which adopted the draft decree will
constitute proof of implementation ofthis measure.

8.       Strengthen and decentralize enterprises' facilities for offering services to developers: The
Maison de 1'Entreprise has since its creation turned out to be a good counseling and service provider for
enterprises. In order to consolidate its action, it has begun a decentralization process aimed at providing
better services to all those setting up business over the national territory. The enhancement of backup
facilities for enterprises shall be deemed accomplished following           : i)the setting up of Business
Development Centers (CEFORE) inthe north and center-east regions; ii)the effective transfer o f one-stop
services to the Muison de 1'Entreprise ;iii)the setting up of the Bobo-Dioulasso Center for the Facilitation
of BuildingPermits (CEFAC).

9.       Have the draft Labor Code adopted by the Council of Ministers and draw up the draft
enactments of application: After the adoption of the labor code, the drawing up of its enactments of
application constitute a crucial phase. The draft enactments of application of the labor code will constitute
the proofthat the measurehas been implemented.

10.      Design and adopt Burkina Faso's exports promotion strategy paper : This measure aims at
designing an overall exports promotion strategy based notably on the diagnostic study              report on
commercial integration for the integrated framework program (EDIC). The availability of this exports
promotion strategy paper in Burkina Faso in 2008 will serve as proof that the measure has been
implemented.

11.      Draft a national quality paper and its action plan that aims at setting up a national
normalization, certification, and accreditationsystem for Burkinabe products: As part of the drive to
step up the competitiveness of the various buoyant sectors of the national economy, the adoption of the
quest for quality is indispensable. Proof of implementation of this measure shall be shown by the
availability of draft national quality policy papers s andtheir action plans.

12.      Finalize the sectoral policy of the Ministry of Commerce, Business and Handicraft
Promotion (MCPEA) to meet diversification challenges and design the draft action plan: This
measure is in response to the need to have a strategic vision and a common framework for all MCPEA


                                                       -115-

policies (statutory and regulatory reforms on the business climate; exports; financial instruments;
institutional capacities; the private sector with an emphasis on SME/SMI, communication strategy). The
availability of the sectoral policy paper and the draft action plan will stand as proof that this measure has
been implemented.

13.     Extend the school funds experience to 45 provincesand their urban councils: The decisions to
releasethese funds will constitutethe proofthat the measure has beenimplemented.

14.      Set up the National Employment and Vocational Training Council: the national council is an
advisory body whose recommendations and opinion guide the government in the making of employment
and vocational training decisions. The setting up of the council shall be proof that this measure will be
implemented in2008.

15.     Develop a strategy for the implementation of the contract policy between the Ministry of
Health and all the structures involved in the health sector: its major objective, on the one hand, is to
encourage the practice of contract arrangements in the health sector and, on the other, to harmonize
contract arrangements with Burkina Faso's national health policy. The availability of the draft strategy
paper for the implementation ofthe contractual policywill be proofof implementation ofthis measure.

16.     Render operational the facility for the monitoringand evaluation of the PN-AEPA: After the
adoption of the national water supply and sanitation policy (PN-AEPA), and in order to ensure a results-
oriented management, it is indispensable to endow the sub sector with an efficient monitoring and
evaluation facility for notably measuringperformance in terms of the rate of access to drinking water and
sanitation infrastructures in the urban and rural areas (indicators 15 and 16).. The adoption by the DGRE
of a timefiame and the provision of human resources and a budget appropriate for rendering operational
the monitoring/ evaluation ofthe PN-AEPA will beproofofthe implementation ofthis measure.

17.     Design the draft bill on Rural Land Tenure based on the National Policy on Land Tenure
Security in the RuralAreas (PNSFMR):The drawing up ofthis draft bill is a follow-up to the PNSFMR
document adopted by Government. The availability of the draft bill on land tenure will be proof of
breakthroughs inthe implementation of this measure.

18.     Ensure the regular functioning of the information system on food and nutrition security
(SISAN) and on food security and interventionstock managementby providingthem with sufficient
resources (at least CFAF 385 million for SISAN in the 2009 appropriation law and CFAF 425
million in that of 2010): The regular functioning of SISAN contributes to the efficient management of
food security. The inclusion of these amounts in the 2009 appropriation law in favor of SISAN, and the
budget execution report for 2008 will serve as proofof implementation ofthis measure.

19.     Adopt the nationalgender policy (PNG)and design relevantaction plan: This measure aims at
an equitable development and equal rights of access to the public service. The minutes of the Council of
Ministersmeeting on the adoption of the PNG and the draft relevant plan for 2008 will constitute proofof
implementation ofthis measure.

20.      Draft a general guideline framework paper for the organization of sectoral supports: The
feasibility report will constitute proofof implementation ofthe measure.

21.     Adopt and implement the 2008-2010 triennial plan of the Strategic Framework for the
Implementation of Decentralization (CSMOD) : The existence of an action plan is essential for
rendering CSMOC operational within a coherent framework while at the same time giving all the players
concerned a clear insight of their role inthe drive to implementthe decentralization process. The adoption
ofthis action planby the Council of Ministersfollowing its validation by CONAD thus constitutesthe first
phase of this initiative. This plan must notably lie down, as its foremost priorities, the concerns expressed
about the transfer of authority and resources to local governments and that of rendering operational the
backup measures put in place, in particular the Standing Fund for the development of Local Authorities



                                                      - 116-

(FPDCT). The core measures to serve as yardsticks for assessing how far the measure has been
implemented will be:

    0   The adoption of memorandums of understanding for the management of services transferred to
        local governments in at least i)49 urban councils, in matters o f basic education ; ii) 100 rural
        councils, in matters of drinkingwater supply and sanitation. The availability o f signed agreements
        inthat wise will constituteproofo f implementation o fthis measure.
    0   The appropriation to local governments in the 2009 appropriation law o f financial resources for
        recurrent expenses (in the field o f basic education) and for rehabilitation investments (in the field
        o f drinking water supply and sanitation), concerning infrastructures and expenses related to the
        powers transferred. Their disbursement shall be on a quarterly basis, as concerns basic education,
        while that o f the water and sanitation sector shall be on the basis o f an annual program based on
        rehabilitation feasibility studies. The effective inclusion o f appropriations inthe 2009 appropriation
        law and the decisions, as well as other documents in proof, showing that these resources are
        available, will constitute proofo f implementation o fthis measure.
    0   The transfer o f at least CFAF 5 billion inthe amended 2008 appropriation law and the provision o f
        at least CFAF 5 billion in the 2009 appropriation law in favor o f FPDCT to meet the investment
        financial needs o f local governments.. Disbursements will be on a quarterly basis.
    0   The share o f resources earmarked for the construction o f school infrastructures in favor o f 13
        (thirteen)headquarter councils o fthe regionswill be transferredto them as from 2009 on the basis
        o f afore agreed upon arrangements. Decisions or other documents inproof showing the availability
        o f these resources and their disbursement every quarter will constitute proof o f implementation o f
        the measure.


22.     Adapt and disseminate regulatory texts and standard documents (Le. sample bid forms
general administrative clauses manual (CCGA) on the new communal and national regulatory
framework for publiccontracts: the clauses and sample and standard documents presently in force come
from 2003 regulations. They have to be adapted within the framework o f a task force. The taking o f
bylaws by the Ministero f the Economy and Finance enacting the new documents into force will constitute
proofthat the measure has been implemented.

23.     Draft a provisionalreport on the nationalstrategy for capacity buildingin procurement: The
renewal o fthe statutory and regulatory framework for public contracts and the difficulties to apply them as
a result o fthe inadequate capacities o f players mean that multiple actions have to be carried out, notably in
the area o f training and the strengthening of institutional capacities. For these actions to be efficient and
coherent, they have to be taken withinthe framework o f a national strategy for capacity buildinginmatters
o f procurement. Proof that this measure has been implemented will be based on the availability o f a
provisional report on the national strategy for capacity buildinginprocurement.

24.     Experiment the procurementinformationsystem (SIMP) in three ministries(MEBA, Health
and MEF) and in two regions: The development o f an information system for public contracts aims at
improving the follow-up o f public contracts through the systematic production o f data useful for
management. This has to be carried out progressively on all the web sites o f users. Statements obtained
from SIMP via the demonstration sites o f the Ministry o f Basic Education and Literacy, Ministry o f
Health, Ministry o f the Economy and Finance and the Hauts Bassins and North regions will stand as proof
that the measure has been implemented.

25.    Publishon line essential informationon public finance: PEFA evaluation revealed a number o f
shortfalls in the making available to the public o f information on public finance, except as concerns public
contracts. What is thus required here i s to place on line validated documents and statistics in order to


                                                        -117-

render the public finance management system more transparent. This measure will be assessed on the basis
o f accessibility on the web site o f the Ministry o f the Economy and Finance o f core budgetary and
accounting information such as: Budget voted (functional classification), monthly table o f State financial
operations, budget execution rate, management accounts, and payment rules, major speeches by the
Minister o f Finance on public finance, funds for local governments (transfers from the central government,
council budgets).

26.     Continue the structural adjustment of the anti corruption facility, especially by rendering
operationalthe Higher State ControlAuthority (ASCE). The adoption o f the decree appointing ASCE
officials, the endowment o f ASCE with human and financial resources that will permit it to act in
accordance with its duties and the availability o f the feasibility report on the attractiveness o f the IGF will
constitute proof o f implementation o fthis measure.
27.     Continue the strengthening of the management capacities of technical and general
inspectorates of ministries and institutions. This entails the sustaining o f the efforts being made to
provide control structures with the logistic and operational means needed for the exercise o f their duties
An SP-PPF report on capacity building activities carried out in 2008 will constitute proof of
implementation o f this measure.
28.     Conduct the 2008 integral survey on the living conditions of households (EICVM): the
availability o fthe survey results will constitute proofo f implementation o fthis measure.

Annex 13: GeneralBudget Support Framework(CGAB-CSLP) Definition of Measuresfor
                                                                   -
2009


Measuresfor 2009:


1. Adopt the draft appropriationlaw for 2010 on the basis of the sector ceilings for the
   overall MTEF for 2010-2012 in line with PRSP priorities: This measure is aimed at
   determining how far Government is willing to translate into concrete reality its commitment
   to implement its poverty reduction program in conformity with the priorities defined in the
   PRSP. Its implementation will be assessed on the basis of a detailed table produced by MEF
   comparing the overall MTEF sectoral financial packages with allocations in the draft 2010
   appropriation law, showing that PRSP priorities such as education, health, rural development,
   etc. have beentaken into account
2. Implement the overall strategy of the fiscal policy, particularlyby adopting and tabling
beforethe NationalAssembly detailedproposalsthe VAT reform, the business tax and the
investmentcode: This measure seeks to broaden the tax base of most taxes, eliminate taxes that
are a nuisance to companies and do not yield much to the tax administration, and simplify the
taxation system. A forwarding slip showing the transmission of this draft bill on reform
proposals to the National Assembly will be proofof implementation ofthis measure.

The continued implementationofthe strategy will focus mainly on:
    -   The revision of the General Tax Code, the reform of the taxation of informal sector
        activities in2010;
    -   The introduction of a tax for agricultural profits in2011.

3. Develop and adopt a strategy for the implantation of the Program Budget and start
implementingit in at least three pilot ministries (MS, MEBA, MAHRH): Program Budgets
are budget programming tools designed to give visibility to the implementation o f sectoral
programs, inthat they show the prospects for resources over a three-year period while improving
the consistency of intra -sectoral allocation of resources with the priorities and programs
adopted in sectoral policies and strategies.. The production of the validated Program Budget
reports for 2010-2012 for the sectors concerned with the deadline of December 31,2009 will be
proofof implementation of this measure.
4. Develop the coherence framework for the productive rural development sectoral
Program PROSDR (p): This activity is part of the drive to develop a productive rural
development program (PROSDRp). The aim o f the program is to ensure the consistency of
investmentsinthe productive rural sector (agriculture, animal resources, environment and living
conditions) and promote a branch-of-activity approach in the rural sector. The coherence
framework should lead to the design of the program budget of the rural development sector. This
measurewill be assessed onthe basis of the availability ofthe coherence framework paper.
5. Develop the TOR for the recruitment of a technical partner of choice for the
managementof the Ouagadougourefrigeratedslaughterhouseand publishthe recruitment
notice: This measure is part of the initiative to improve the operating conditions of the AFO, in
order to increase, on the one hand, its use for slaughtering and exporting meat, to the detriment
of cattle on the hoof, and on the other, its attractiveness to the private sector. Its implementation

                                                -124  -

will be supported by the World Bank through the project in support of the agro-pastoral and
forestry sectors (PAFASP) in terms o f standards. Proof o f Government's commitment will be
shown by the availability o f the terms o f reference and the publication o f the notice for the
recruitment o f the technical partner o f choice.
6. Develop a 2009-2011 three-year action plan for the restructuring and support of the
cotton sector: monitoring of the implementation of this plan will be provided by Government
through the establishment o f quarterly performance reports. This plan should contain measures to
improve productivity (including a policy for the supply o f inputs), work out, as well as those to
enhance SOFITEX's performance. The adoption by the end o f September 2009 o f the action
plan by the Council of Ministers and its implementation shown in the quarterly performance
report will be proof o f implementation o f this measure
7.     Formalize the consultation framework for stakeholders and partners in the cotton
sector: The aim o f the effective introduction of a consultation framework for stakeholders and
partnersinthe cotton sector des, that will meet on a quarterlybasis, is to share information on the
implementation status o f the strategy to end the crisis, the three-year action plan and discuss the
sector's prevailing situation.. The availability o f a text by Government creating and defining the
functioning o f the consultation framework will be proof o f implementation o f this measure.
8.       Develop at least 2 (two) sectoral e-strategies to promote the integrationof ICT in
sectoral development policies: The availability of two sectoral e-strategies will be proof o f
completion o f this activity.

9.         Develop an integratedsystem for the managementof CEFORE activities and set
up CEFOREs in the Center-North, East, Center-West and South-West regions: The
"Maison de 1'Entreprise" has since its creation appeared to be a good source o f advice and
services to businesses. In order to strengthen its actions, it has embarked on a decentralization
process to better serve entrepreneurs throughout the country. The extent o f the attending
measures in support o f businesses will be assessed through: i)the effective establishment o f a
functional management system and; ii)the creation o f Business Formalities Centers (CEFORE)
in the Centre-North, East, Centre-West and South-West regions ( via the texts creating the
centers andthe appointment o f officials).

10.     Support the implementation of the priority measures of the strategy plan of the
Maisonde 1'Entreprisedu BurkinaFaso (MEBF), by grantingit the status of publicutility:
This is to ensure the sustainability o f the institution. The implementationo f this measure will be
evidenced by the adoption by Government o f the draft bill grantingit the status o f public utility.

11.      Support the implementation of the priority measures of the strategy plan of the
Maison de 1'Entreprise du Burkina Faso (MEBF), in order to ensure the structure's
sustainability, by issuing it a title deed (land title): This measure aims at ensuring the
sustainability o f the institution. The implementation o f this measure will be evidenced by the
availability o f the bylaws by the MEF permanently granting MEBF the built-on piece o f land
indicated in the land title issued by the council in which the institution's headquarters are
located.

12.      Support the implementation of the priority measures of the strategy plan of the
Maison de 1'Entreprisedu Burkina Faso (MEBF) with a view to ensuringthe structure's
sustainability,by setting up a capacity building fund for the private sector: This measure



                                                - 125-

seeks to ensure the Institution's sustainability. The implementation of this measure will be
evidenced by the availability of the text setting up the fund.

13.    Developan actionplanfor implementingthe overallstrategy for promotingBurkina
Faso's exports: This measure seeks to render operational the overall strategy for promoting
exports currently being developed on the basis, in particular, of the Diagnostic Study on trade
integration for the integrated framework program (EDIC). The availability of the action plan
document in2009 will be evidence of implementation ofthis measure.
14.          Develop the national policy paper on quality and its draft plan of action for
establishing a national system of standardization, certification and accreditation for
Burkina Faso products: As part of the drive to improve the competitiveness of the various
buoyant sectors of the national economy, the adoption of quality standards i s essential for the
conquest of domestic, regional and international markets.. The implementation of this measure
will be evidenced by the adoption by the Council of Ministers of a national policy paper on
quality and the availability of the draft action plan.

15.          Adopt the sectoral policy paper of the Ministry of Commerce, Business and
Handicraft Promotion(MCPEA) and develop its action plan :This measure seeks to meet
the challengesposedby the diversification of the economy and respondto the needfor a strategic
vision and a unifying framework for MCPEA's policies and strategies (legal reforms on the
business climate, exports, Burkina Faso standards and label, funding instruments, institutional
capacities, the private sector with a focus on SMEBMI, communication strategy). Adoption by
the Council of Ministers of the sectoral policy paper and the availability of its action planwill be
proofof implementation ofthis measure.

16.     Adopt the subsector policy for Secondary and Higher Education and Scientific
Research and develop its draft action plan: This measure is part of Government's
commitment to provide all sectors with a sectoral policy. The availability of the sectoral policy
paper adopted by the Council of Ministers and the draft action plan will be evidence of
implementation of this measure.

17.      Adopt and put in place a facility for rendering operational and carrying out the
monitoring-evaluationof the strategy of contracts between the Ministry of Health and all
the structures involvedin the healthfield and start its implementation:this measuremainly
seeks, on the one hand, to encourage the practice of contracting in the health sector and, on the
other, to harmonize contractual arrangements with the national health policy of Burkina Faso.
The adoption by the Council of Ministers of the strategy paper for the implementation of the
contractual policy and the report on the implementation o f the strategy will be proof of
implementation of the measure.

18.   Validate the 2009-2011programbudget of the Water and Sanitationsector and take
into account itsfundinginMAHRH priorities:This is to allow the integration ofthe priorities
of the ((water and sanitation   ))subsector in MAHRH's programming through, especially, the
ministry's program budget and the intra-sectoral budgetary allocations. The validated program
budget will be evidence of implementation of this measure.

19.   Have the Council of Ministers adopt the draft bill on rural land tenure and table it
before the NationalAssembly: The development of the draft bill is a follow-up to the national
policy paper on securing landtenure inthe rural areas (PNSFMR) adopted by Government. The
minutes of the Council of Ministers on the adoption of the draft bill on rural landtenure and the


                                                - 126-

slip attesting to the forwarding of the draft bill to the NationalAssembly will constitute proof of
implementation of this measure.

20.      Ensure the proper functioning of the information system on food and nutrition
security (SISAN) and the managementof food security and emergency stocks by allocating
adequate resources of at least 385 million CFA francs for SISAN and one billion CFA francs for
the security stock in the 2009 appropriation law, and 425 million CFA francs and one billion
CFA francs respectively in the 2010 appropriation law. The smooth functioning of SISAN
contributes to the efficient management of food security. The inclusion of these amounts in the
2010 appropriation law, for SISAN and the performance report for 2009 will serve as proof of
implementation of this measure.

21.          Develop a support plan for the national gender policy (PNG) and start its
implementation:The purpose of this measure is to develop equitable and equal rights of access
to public services. The minutes of the Council of Ministers on the adoption of the support plan
for the PNG will serve as proof of its implementation in2009.

22.     Include in the 2010 appropriationlaw the financial resources to be transferred, on
the one hand, to the FPDCT, and, on the other, to local authorities for recurrent costs,
includingschoolfunds, in the area of basiceducation         ,and for rehabilitationinvestmentsin
the AEPA area, concerninginfrastructureand expenses relatedto the powerstransferred:
This measure is part of the program to implementthe three-year planof the Strategy Framework
for the implementation of decentralization (CSM0D)particularly its axis no2 concerning the
transfer of powers and resources. As regards the FPDCT, the issue here i s the transfer of at least
5 billion into the Fund to support the investment financing needs of local authorities.
Disbursementwill be on a quarterly basis for the FPDCT and the basic education and water and
sanitation sectors. The effective allocation of these funds in the 2010 appropriation law and the
decisions and other justifying documents showing that the said funds have been made available
will be evidence of implementation ofthis measure.

23. Transfer with effect from 2010 of the resources programmedfor the construction of
school infrastructure in 49 (forty-nine) urban councils, on the basis of established
agreements: This measure falls within the framework of the program to implement the three-
year plan of the Strategy framework for the implementation of decentralization (CSMOD), in
particular, its axis 2 concerning the transfer of powers and resources. Decisions or other
documents showing proof of the availability of these resources and their disbursement on a
quarterly basis will be evidence of implementation of this measure.

24. DesignCouncilDevelopmentPlans, includingthe drinkingwater and wastewater and
excreta treatment sectoral dimension (PCD-AEPA), for 269 Burkina Faso councils, and
include an allocation of 300 million in the 2010 appropriation law : This measure is part of
the drive to implement the three-year plan of the Strategy Framework for the Implementation of
Decentralization (CSMOD) in particular, its axis 4 concerning supports for the design and
implementation of council developmentplans. The availability o f PCD-AEPA documents for the
211 councils and the inclusion of the allocation of 300 million inthe State budget for 2010 will
beproofof implementation of the measure.

25.             Enhance budget transparency at the level of local authorities through the
publication on the Government's website, at the start of the fiscal year, of the budgetary
allocations for the year and the performance data for year n-2, by section and heading, o f the 49


                                              - 127 -

 (forty-nine) councils in 2009. These data could be used for communication with the population
via appropriate channels such as public notices, inparticular.
26.       Pursue the devolution of the DGMP in three ministries(MAHRH, MID, MESSRS)
 and three new regions(Mouhoun, East and Sahel) :the goal here i s to encourage diligence in
the control o f files by appointing within the contracting Authorities, procurement specialists that
have acquired experience within the Directorate General o f Procurement Contracts. This
 devolution should be accompanied by the provision o f the necessary operational means,
 including the extension o f SIMP, inorder to improve the monitoring o f Procurement contracts by
 systematically    producing useful    management      data. The     decrees appointing       DGMP
representatives and the report on the implementation o f the SRFP showing that funds are
 available will be proof o f implementationo f the measure.
27. Enhance transparency of public finances by improving access by the public to
 information: The PEFA assessment has identified gaps in the information o f the public on
public finances, except as regards information on public procurement. The target here i s to make
 available on the net documents and validated statistics in order to enhance the transparency o f
the public financial management system. This measure will be assessed on the basis o f the
 accessibility on the Government's websites o f essential budgetary and accounting information
 (in a simpliJed format and understandable by the general public) : Budget voted (economic and
functional classification according to headings), monthly table on the State's financial
transactions, monthly statement o f budget execution, management accounts o f the State's
principal accountants and payment regulations, major speeches by the Minister o f Finance on
public finances.
28.        Review the national policy against corruption and adopt an action plan in
consultationwith all stakeholders:This review aims to take into account, on the one hand, the
deficiencies inthe original version and, on the other, the new institutional context marked by the
creation o f ASCE to replace HACLC and IGE. The availability o f the revised policy paper and
the actionplanwill beproofofimplementationofthis measure.
29. Strengthenservice controlby the DGCF. :This measure i s designed to extend the scope
o f coverage o f the control exercised by the DGCF, by making use o f its decentralized services.
This will be assessed on the basis o f the logistics available, the humanresources provided and
the ad hoc control teams set up to lend support to the new directorate in charge o f physical
control and services.. The DGCF will, to this end, produce a report on the implementation o f the
capacity building activities cited above.
30.          Set up a Chamber of budgetary and financialdisciplinewithin the State Audit
Office and start investigating cases: A report by the State Audit Office on the creation o f a
Chamber o f budgetary and financial discipline and the start o f its activities will constitute proof
o f implementation o f this measure. For 2010-2011, evidence as to its implementation will be
jointly decided in collaboration with the State Audit Office, in accordance with the regulations
andprocedures inforce.
31.          Continue the Comprehensive Survey of the Living Conditions of Households
(EICVM) : This survey will enable Government to have more complete information on
households, thereby providing it with a better knowledge o f living conditions, the health o f
children and mothers, the HIV/AIDS situation, the reasons that underlie population movement,
and the employment and education situation. The choice o fthis survey stemmed from the needto


                                               -128 -

address the concern raised by the multidimensional nature of poverty. The survey will contain
variables generated by the QUIBB, EBCVM and EDS module. The statistical program includes
plans to continue the comprehensive survey of the living conditions of households (EICVM),
with results expected in 2010. The availability of the results of the survey from the QUIBB
module will be proofof implementation ofthe measurein2009.
