   Annex 15: GeneralBudget Support Framework(CGAB-CSLP) - Definition of Indicators for 2008

2008 indicators:

1.       Rate of realization of fiscal revenue
This is a confirmation of the pertinence of the targets referred to in the appropriation law, to
show the credibility o f this policy instrument that the budget represents. However, it was
decided that this indicator should be completed with reference to the objectives spelt out inthe
PRGF program, as these are indications o f government commitments to ensure the stability o f
the macroeconomic framework which constitute the basic condition for PTFs involved in
Overall Budget Support. The objective should however remain that o f sooner or later reducing
the gaps that exist between the figures o f the appropriation law and those o f the PRGF, so as to
further enhance the credibility o f the appropriation law.
              Rate of realization of fiscal revenue in comparison to            appropriation law
              estimates :
Itis calculated by comparing "fiscal revenue" realizations as at end o fDecember, at the close
                                                            ))
of the extra day (February 28 o f the following year), to the initial appropriation law estimates,
in accordance with TOFE nomenclature. In carrying out this calculation, it is recommended
that the capital losses noticed in the Communal Preferential Tax, (TPC) and not offset by the
West African Economic and Monetary Union (UEMOA) should not be included in the
indicator, so as not to skew the series from one year to another.
The sources o f data denominator for the calculation o f this indicator are the revenue estimates
included in the appropriation law (reclassified according to the TOFE nomenclature) while
those o f the numerator are the realizations included inthe TOEF at the end o f the year, at the
close o f the extra day, (February 28).

         0   Rate of realization of fiscal revenue incomparison to the PRGF program
It is calculated inthe same way as above, except that the denominator data sources are PRGF
program estimates.


2.      Budget allocations for priority sectors (health, basic education, finance and
budget) exclusive of debts, tax exemptions, externally financed projects and national
compensation for externally financed projects
The objectives are indicated in the C D T M project and their implementation i s verified in the
initial appropriation law adopted by the National Assembly (and, as the case may be, in the
amended appropriation laws).


3.      Budget execution rate (payment phase)
The budget execution rate o f the ministries concerned is calculated by comparing the
expenditures made by the ministry (payment basis) to expenditure estimates o f the initial
appropriation law (and, as the case may be, in the amended appropriation laws) (exclusive o f
external financing). Calculations are carried out on the basis o f the data at the close of the extra



                                               - 134-

day (at February 28 o f the following year). Data sources for the calculation o f this indicator are
the ExpenditureComputerizedNetwork andthe appropriation law for the year.


4.      Processing time for legally starting a business (in business days) and Cost of
startinga business
This indicator will have two sources o f information: the annual report Doing Business            ((     ))and
the report of the Sectoral and Thematic Commission charged with the promotion o f the private
sector and competitiveness.
According to   ((Doing Business    D,  the indicator contains the upstream timeframes for starting a
business, that is to say, the steps for opening an account, obtaining a police record, getting the
business registered at the taxation department (.,.) and identifying the administrative and
statutory bottlenecks that an entrepreneur has to face inhis bidto start a business. It studies the
relevant procedures, timeframes and cost for starting a business or an industrial firm with less
than 50 employees, and endowed with an initial capital 10 times the gross per capita national
income (GNI). It obtains information by means o f a questionnaire addressed to the major legal
offices of each country coveredby the annual survey                     (( Doing Business          D.
As concerns the Government, the indicator shows the processing time for administrative
formalities for starting business with the assistance o f Centers for Business Formalities
(CEFORE) and the relevant cost. The entrepreneur is given information on the average time
needed for processing files by CEFORE.


5.      Reducingthe employmentrigidityimpact
As indicated inthe   ((Doing Business        ))  report, its trend i s a reflection o f the measures taken to
scale up the flexibility o f the labor market. It measures the difficulties for recruiting a new
employee, the rigidity o f the rules governing the extension o f working hours or reaching an
agreement on work schedules, non wage labor costs linked to the recruitment o f an employee,
and the difficulties and the cost linked to the economic dismissal o f a wage earner. It obtains
information through an annual survey o f a cross section o f workers and businessmen by a
consultant chosen by the WB. It i s recommended that the national plan be followed by a
second indicator such as the growth trend o f cases declared via the number o f wage earners
declared to the CNSS This will show the impact o f this flexibility o f employment. Data
producedby the CNSS will provide the indicator with information.


6.     Gross EnrollmentRate is the number of pupils attending (public and private) primary
schools in comparison to the population o f school age (7 to 12 year children), expressed in
percentage.
                                            Total number o f pupils inprimary school
               GER = lOO*------------------------------------------------------------------------
       (Gross schooling rate)               Total population o f 7-12 years o f age


               Source: DEP/MEBA- annual statistics directories.



                                                          - 135     -

7.      Gross EnrollmentRate (GER) of girls measuresaccess into primary school year one
as well as the capacity of the system to admit into class 1 (CP1) childrenof school age. It can
be calculated according to gender, the type of geographic unit (region, province, and division,
urban or rural area).
The gross registration rate for the CP1 is equal to the number of new registrations for the CP1
divided by the number of childrenfulfilling the legal admission age (7 years).
                      Total number of girl pupils inthe CP1- Number of girls repeatingthe class
GER girls =     loo* ........................................................................................
                                           Total population of 7 year old children
                 Source :DEP/MEBA - statistics directories

8.      System's efficiency
                 Pupils per teacher : This is the number of pupils per teacher in (both public
                 and private) primary school classes
                          Number ofpupils attending primary school (both public andprivate)
                 REM=.....................................................................................
                                 Numberofteachers (inbothpublic andprivate schools)
The arithmetic book per pupiland the readingbook per pupil:These indicatorshelpto
determine how many school books each pupil has.


9.      Schoolcompletionrate in(%)
This indicator measures the efficiency of the school system. It shows how many childrenhave
attained class 7 (CM2) at the normal age. The completion rate is the number of CM2 pupilsnot
repeating class (inboth public andprivate schools) comparedto 12 year old children expressed
inpercentage

       Completionrate= 100          *(Number of    CM2 pupils-Number of pupilsrepeating CM2)
                                      ________________________________________----_---------------------    -_____
                                                    Total number of 12year old children
                 Source :DEP/MEBA - statistics directory

10.    Percentageof CSPS respectingstaff norms
At the level of Health and Social Promotion Centers (CSPS), staff norm is as follows: (i)                       A
State RegisteredNurse (IDE) or a Staff Nurse (IB), (ii) Assistant Midwife (AA), and (iii)
                                                                   an                                            a
mobile health worker (AIS).
The indicator is calculated by comparing the number of CSPS abiding by this norm, to the
number ofCSPS. Staff financed bythe State budget as well as local governmentsare taken into
account.

11.    Rateof qualified staffassisted deliveries(in %)
This indicator measures the proportion of deliveries assisted by health personnel in health
units. It i s calculated by comparing the total number of births handled by health workers to the
total number of expecteddeliveries.



                                                    - 136-

12.    Vaccination rate
The antigen vaccination coverage rate for a given vaccine is the comparison between the
number of children of the given age who have received the vaccine, and the total number of
children of the same age group. The recommendedantigens are the DTC-HEP-HB3, VAR.

Source: This indicator is monitored every month as part of the Extended Program of
Immunizationof the Ministry of Health. M.SANTE/DEP -Annual statistics directory.


13.    Percentage of MEGwarehouses that have not been out of stock
This concernsthe number of stores that have notbeen out of stock of the 10most useddrugs in
comp&ison to the total number of stores.
Source: SNIS report and statistics directory M.SANTE / DEP.


14.    Number of new consultations per year
This indicator shows the accessibility to and acceptability ofhealth care by the population. It is
thus an indirect indicator of the quality of services provided. It measuresethenumber of new
consultants per person per year in first class structures (CSPS, CMA). 0.37 means 37 new
consultants per 100 people per year. It does not take into account private sector activities and
only partially reflects population demands for healthcare.
Source: SNIS report and statistics directory M.SANTE / DEP.


15.    Rate of access to drinkingwater
The rate of access i s defined as the proportion of the rural population having a modern water
point (PEM) less than 1000m from its quarterhamlet of residence, with a maximum
population density of 300 persons per PEM or a water fountain at less than 500m, with a
maximum population density of 600 persons per drinking fountain.
Datasources: DGFWMAHRH.
Baseyear: 2005.


16.    Rate of access to sanitation infrastructures
The rate of access to sanitation is defined as the proportion of the rural population having
adequate structures for the management o f sewage and excreta, to the tune o f 10 persons per
structure.

Data sources: DGRE/MAHRH.
Base vear: 2005.




                                              -137  -

17.     Trend of hydro-agricultural farms to develop (in ha/yr)
             Lowlands: It i s a privileged area in a geographic setting where flowing rain water
             concentrates with a rather large distribution, depending on the area's topography.
             The development of lowland allows for a more rational use of outflows for the
             cultivation o f a wide range o f products.
        0    Small and medium size perimeters: these are farms o f at most 100 hectares. They
             are situated downstream to dams, around natural lakes and on the banks o f
             perennial rivers. They are developed either by means o f a water source or by
             means o f an irrigation network
        0    Large and medium size farms: These are agricultural farms that cover several
             thousand hectares at a stretch. The development o f these farms requires substantial
             investments.

Data sources: DEP/MAHRH.
Base year: 2006


18.     Number of rural roads built (in km)
This indicator makes it possible to monitor the effort being made by Government to open up
rural areas so as to facilitate access by the rural population to urban areas. It also helps to
determine the growth trend o f the number o f rural roads built by SOFITEX for the transport o f
cotton products to the ginningareas.

Data sources: General Directorate o fRural Roads (DGPWID).
Base year: 2006.

19.     Electrification rate
Apart from the global rate, this indicator also makes it possib,,:    to   llow up that o f rural
electrification thanks to statistics provided by the DGEo f the MMCE.
Data sources: General Directorate o f Energy
Base year: 2006


20.     Percentageof State budget transferred to local governments(regions and councils)
This indicator measures the financial efforts made by the State towards local governments, on
the strength o f its own budget, exclusive o f debts, tax exemptions, externally financed projects
and compensations for projects. It also includes transfers to structures charged with the
management o f the decentralization process such as the national decentralization commission,
the local development fund, council associations, the national twinningcommittee, etc.
 Method o f calculation: sum total for heads 11, 111, IV and V transferred to local governments,
compared to total budget expenditures for above headings.
For heads 11, I11and IVYsee section 9 above.
For head V, see section 9 and DCIM.




                                                 -138-

21.     Shareof publiccontractsconcludedwithinthe bid's timeframe
The aim of this indicator is to measure the efficiency of procurement services, both at the
global level and as concerns certain key sectorsto betargeted each year.
Method of calculation: Compare the number of contracts concluded withinthe bid's timeframe
with the total number of contracts concluded within the base period, namely the financial year
or the calendar year.


22.     Breakdown of public contracts per procurement procedure (open tender,
restrictedtender, mutualconsent, delegatedcontractingauthority [MOD])
This involves the measuring of the extent to which exceptional proceduresare used, andwhose
reduction will be an indicationof government efforts to scale up transparency inthis sector.
The assessment of this measure will be based on the statistics produced by the General
Directorate of Public Contracts.


23.     Production and transmission deadlines for management accounts and draft bills
on payments
The government must at all time see to the respect of these deadlines, in accordance with the
prescriptions laid down inthe UEMOA commission's communal guidelines. The transmission
notes of management accounts to the State Audit Office and the draft bill on payments to the
National Assembly will standas proof of implementation of this measure.
    J Senior accountants handling the State budget are three in number: (i)the General
        Paymaster (PG); (ii)   the Central Treasury's Accountant (ACCT); and (iii) General
                                                                                    the
        Tax-Collector. Each accountant has to produce eachyear his management accounts for
        the financial year (N) before June 30 of year (Nt-1). The said accounts have to be
        forwarded to the State Audit Office for examination and decision.
    J   The (N) accounts of senior accountants are approved in order to obtain the overall
        Treasury balance of (N),which is normally produced before June 30 (N+l).
    J June 30 constitutesthe regulatory deadlineto be set as the target deadline for turning in
        management accounts and September 30 as that of forwarding to the State Audit Office
        and the NationalAssembly the Bill on payments.


24.     Publicreportby the HigherStateControlAuthority (ASCE)
The report by the ASCE shall be published with due account being taken, in keeping with
international norms thereon, of the exercise of its core duties (anti-corruption investigations,
production o f basic statistics on the number of corruption cases and the examination of reports
by control bodies). The delay inlaunching its activities will have an impact on the 2008 report.


25.     Scope, nature and monitoringof external auditvia the State Audit Office's public
reportThis indicator correspondsto indicator 26 of the PEFA and has beenadoptedas part of
the findings of the public finance enhancement strategy. External audit is carried out by the
State Audit Office which constitutes a part of the Bench. The rating scale provided by PEFA
will be used to assess the trend of the indicator in terms of progress made in its three


                                              - 139 -

components, namely: i)Extent o f the control (accounts control and administrative control); ii)
deadlines for the presentation o f reports; and iii)monitoring o f recommendations. The public
report by the State Audit Office will, as part o f the Office's public finance control duties,
report on the trend o fthese components.
The global objective i s the scaling up o f PEFA ratings over the next three years (Cf. table
below). Inorder to assess the second component on presentation deadlines, account has to be
taken o fthe regulatory and statutory framework inforce thereon. Following the first control in
2007, the principle o fhaving independent experts conduct an assessment o fPEFA every 3 years
was adopted. The State Audit Office shall betweentwo PEFA sessions be assessedby its peers
(withthe first beingin2009), inaccordance withthe practice inforce within these institutions
andthe indicator shall, annually, be assessedby SRFP, a technical control group, which shall
define the terms and conditions. It should be noted that the indicator will cover the exercise by
DGTCP o f the powers delegated to it by the State Audit Office to audit local governments for
budgets o f less than CFAF 20 million.

Targets drawn from PAST-SRFP:

    audit:
 0  Percentageof State structures audited             D      D

    National Assembly (general statement of           C      C
    conformity)

P PP




26.    IGFauditedcontracts (innumber andvalue)
This indicator takes into account as "public contracts      D:letter commands and State budget
contracts with no external financing.
Ittakes into account two dimensions:
    J The number of auditedpublic contracts:       this concerns the number of letter commands
       and contracts (procurement, performance and materiality) effectively audited by the
       general inspectorate o f finance duringthe given year.
    J Theshare in value ofpublic contracts is calculated      by comparing the value o f contracts
       audited by the general inspectorate o f finance (IGF) with the total value in percentage
       o f contracts signed during the year under review. To calculate this, data has to be
       obtained from the IGF, as concerns the total value o f audited contracts, and from the
       DCMP, as concerns the total value o f contracts duringthe year under review.
    J At the end of the fiscal year, the    IGF finalizes a report presenting all the audits carried
       out, the shortfalls noticed, and the core recommendations made. The report must also
       contain the list o f contracts (number and value), and the list o f audited contracts
       (number and value).




                                              -  140-

27.    Corruptionrating:this rating shows the level of corruption inthe public sector in 180
countries and territories. This composite rating is basedon several surveys and polls conducted
by independent bodies. Countries are ranked according to a scale ranging from zero (high
degree o f corruption) to ten (low degree of corruption).
